Liu Hongsheng and Others Return to Shanghai, Agreement Reached on Water-Land Intermodal Transport Case 131

When the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was handling the intermodal transport of the Longhai Railway on the Lao Yao Road, there was no conflict because there were few relationships with foreign shipping companies. After the continued realization of intermodal transport on the Jiaoji Railway and the Pinghan Railway, it aroused the aversion of foreign shipping companies in Shanghai, because the foreign shipping companies' voyages, tonnage, and business on the Yangtze River and the north-south ocean routes were larger than those of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. After the implementation of water-land intermodal transport, the goods transported from the railway were not loaded on foreign ships at all. The foreign merchants had to seek a way to save the situation because their business was greatly affected. The only way was to reduce the water freight. Wherever there was intermodal transport, the freight was reduced to even cheaper than the intermodal transport rate. The water freight from Hankou was reduced to only a few yuan per ton.

Foreign Merchants' Demands

It is not a fundamental plan for the foreign shipping companies to compete for voyages by reducing fees. If they hold on like this, they will suffer losses from each other. Therefore, the foreign shipping companies in Shanghai, such as Butterfield & Swire and Jardine Matheson, have discussed it several times. As a result, they decided to use the Washington Nine-Power Treaty as a reason to make demands on us and join our country's water-land intermodal transport in order to obtain the benefits of distributing the national freight. The foreign merchants then submitted this intention to the governments of their respective countries, and the governments ordered their ministers to China to make a formal request to our Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

Two-Ministry Meeting

After receiving this request, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs consulted with the Ministry of Transportation and the Ministry of Railways for verification. The ministers of the two ministries telegraphed to Shanghai to convene representatives of state-owned and private shipping companies to go to Beijing for a public meeting. Liu Hongsheng, general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Zhou Fengtu, director of the intermodal transport division, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Zhiyi of the Sanbei Company, Yuan Ludeng of the NingShao Company, Yang Guanbei of the Dada Company, and Li Zhiyi and Zhu Angsheng of other companies went to Beijing last Friday. On Saturday, a meeting was held at the Ministry of Transportation, and the Ministry of Railways also sent representatives to attend, and the matter was brought up for public discussion.

Decision on Measures

Liu Hongsheng, Zhou Fengtu, Li Zhiyi, Yuan Ludeng, Xu Zhiyi, etc. returned to Shanghai from Beijing yesterday, and Yu Qiaqing turned to the Beijing-Hangzhou Road to go to Ningbo. According to those who came from Beijing and Shanghai, the foreign shipping companies' request to participate in water-land intermodal transport was based on the Washington Nine-Power Treaty, and especially on the reason that the private shipping companies could participate. After discussion by the representatives present, it was decided that water-land intermodal transport was originally a connection between our country's state-owned railways and state-owned shipping, for the convenience of merchants and the reduction of transport rates and procedures. It was purely our country's internal affairs, and foreign merchants had no reason to make demands. Therefore, it was decided on the spot to refuse. As for the participation of Shanghai's private shipping companies, it was also agreed that they could only be affiliated with the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. The dispatch of ships and the loading of goods were all controlled by the bureau. No other joint office was allowed to be established by the private shipping companies to justify their name and avoid excuses.

Today's Polish Community Celebrates Piłsudski 132

Name Day Anniversary of the National Rebuilder, Meeting Held at the American Women's Association

At 6:30 PM today, all Polish residents in Shanghai will hold a celebration meeting at the American Women's Association at 577 Jing'an Temple Road. Polish Minister Wietow will attend and deliver a speech. General Piłsudski is the founding hero of Poland and has won the unanimous support of the whole country. He was born on December 5, 1867, in the small village of Zułów in northern Poland. He is now 68 years old. He studied medicine at a Russian university. At that time, Poland was divided by Russia, Germany, and Austria. Piłsudski's patriotic ideas were unusually strong. He gathered like-minded young people and often thought of restoring the freedom of his motherland. The Russian government sent police to closely monitor his actions. In 1887, he was sentenced to five years in prison and exiled to Siberia. When he returned after his term, he still gathered his former comrades to secretly carry out patriotic work. In 1894, he founded the Workers' Daily, which was secretly sold to promote the restoration of the country. In the end, he was chased by the authorities and fled to London. He met the current Polish President Ignacy Mościcki and made an unbreakable friendship. Piłsudski knew that the European War was about to break out and recognized this as an excellent opportunity to create Polish independence. He went to Kraków to organize a volunteer army. More and more people returned, and the momentum gradually increased. During the European War, Piłsudski used this volunteer army to resist Russia and fought for Polish independence, winning successive victories. Later, Germany and Austria wanted to use his volunteer army, but Piłsudski refused. In 1917, he was imprisoned by the German government in an army prison. The following year, the Great War ended and he was released. Poland also finally gained freedom with Piłsudski's efforts. Piłsudski immediately returned to his country to organize the government and sort out various military and political plans. He was elected as the leader of the provisional government. When the formal constitution was completed, although he was elected as the first president, he firmly declined and retreated to the position of Minister of Military Affairs, actively reorganizing the army. The military appearance became stronger day by day. In 1920, the Russian army that invaded Poland was repelled, and his reputation became more prominent. He was regarded as one of the strongest armies in the world. Poland has reached today mostly due to Piłsudski's contribution. Therefore, the whole country sings his praises endlessly. Today's commemoration, all Polish residents in the country and overseas unanimously hold grand celebrations.

China Aviation Company's Large Ford Aircraft's Test Flight Result is Satisfactory, Shanghai-Yunnan Route Scheduled to Open 133

According to the Shen Times News Agency, the China Aviation Company's newly purchased large Ford aircraft has been shipped from the United States to Shanghai last week. After being assembled at Longhua Airport, it was originally scheduled to conduct a test flight on the 16th of this month. However, the company, with the Shanghai-Yunnan route urgently waiting to be opened, could not delay it for a long time. Therefore, the test flight work was held in the sky near Longhua Airport at 11:00 AM on the 17th. The company's chief pilot, Mr. Le Erxun, drove it and continued to fly in the sky for half an hour. Although it was a stomach rain flight on that day, the results were very good. At 11:30 AM, it landed safely at Longhua Airport. Yesterday, it was determined by the China Aviation Company that the test flight results of the Ford aircraft were excellent. It has now been decided to conduct a second test flight from Shanghai to Yunnan this weekend or early next week. The aircraft will first fly from Shanghai to Chongqing, and then take off from there through a mountainous section of the journey. If everything goes well at that time, the company has decided to officially open the route on January 1st. In the first month of opening the route, it will not carry passengers for the time being, only mail and packages, to ensure safety.

Bravery: The Bold Exploits of Three Young Men 135

Recovering Sunken Gold from a Sailing Vessel

According to the Shanghai Times, Mr. Gates, an American residing in Shanghai, aged 28, Mr. Rawling, aged 21, and Mr. Ritter, a German residing in Shanghai, aged 26, have planned to sail the 33-foot sailing vessel "Flying Dutchman" on April 1st. They will embark on a 15,000-mile journey to Cocos Island in the Indian Ocean to search for sunken gold. It is said that during the European War, the German cruiser Emden was sunk in that location by the Australian cruiser Sydney. The Emden had reportedly roamed the seas for months, attacking and seizing many ships, accumulating a significant amount of gold. Furthermore, in 1520, a Spanish merchant ship carrying millions of dollars in gold coins sank approximately 800 miles from Luderitz Bay in Southwest Africa. Six years ago, Mr. Ritter accidentally discovered its location. If they can find it, they are certain to return laden with treasure. The three young men estimate that the mission will take about a year. Along the way, they plan to first stop at the northern coast of Taiwan to stock up on supplies. Then, they will head to Babuyan Island off the northern coast of Luzon. It is said that the island has many women, with only one man for every twenty women. The three young men intend to investigate the truth of this claim. Next, they will pass through the Philippine Islands to explore gold mines in New Guinea. If they find anything, they plan to acquire equipment to harvest pearls in the world-renowned pearl-producing area off the northern coast of Australia. They also intend to explore Komodo Island, which is rumored to be inhabited by monstrous dragons and giant beasts. The three young men hope to capture their images. Mr. Gates previously served as an officer in the U.S. Navy, and Mr. Ritter recently worked as the Shanghai representative of a German maritime news agency. Mr. Rawling can dive to a depth of 60 feet without diving gear. Although their ship is small, it is very sturdy and comfortable, equipped with the latest navigational instruments. They will set sail under the German flag. Such young men can truly be described as embodying the spirit of adventure.

Silk Industry Bank Invites Zhang Naiqi to Speak on Financial Issues, Titled "Basic Conditions of Modern Financial Markets" 141

The Shanghai Silk Industry Bank holds academic lectures from time to time to enhance the knowledge of its employees. Yesterday, it was time for the regular meeting, and the bank specially invited the famous economic expert Zhang Naiqi to give a lecture entitled "Basic Conditions of Modern Financial Markets." More than one hundred employees from the head office and branches attended the lecture, which was chaired by the bank's general manager, Wang Yansong. After the chairman gave an introductory speech, Mr. Zhang began his lecture. First, he stated that the task of the financial industry is to ensure the full circulation of funds in the market. Although the financial industry in our country has done its best to promote circulation in the past, it has not achieved the goal of full circulation. Its contribution is not enough to meet the actual needs of modern financial markets. Next, he mentioned the outdated investment methods of the financial industry as the main cause of financial panic. In the past, the lending methods of the financial industry were limited to two types: personal credit and property credit. Most of the loans obtained by industry and commerce from the financial industry were converted into accounts receivable from customers. As a result, what the banking industry obtained was the accounts receivable of industry and commerce, and what industry and commerce obtained was the accounts receivable of customers. Since these debts could not be transferred or mortgaged, the limited funds on the market were trapped in a stagnant stalemate, and market panic occurred. Finally, Mr. Zhang advocated that the financial industry should (1) complete a modern money market so that industry and commerce can obtain financing for working capital through bill discounting; (2) complete a modern capital market by converting all loans and mortgages from the financial industry to factories into the issuance of corporate stocks and bonds, so that the accounts receivable owned by themselves become securities that can be circulated and transferred. At the same time, it is necessary to improve the inherent money market and further provide industry and commerce with financing. As a result of the dual expansion of credit funds, it will not only be enough to save the temporary financial panic but also establish a permanent economic system. Mr. Zhang's narrative lasted for more than an hour, and the meeting adjourned at about 8 o'clock.

The Shanghai General Labor Union has recently received petitions from workers of various factories, such as the Shenxin No. 2 and No. 5 factories, Huafeng Flour Mill, and Minsheng Yarn Factory, stating that due to the factories' announcements of closure, the workers' livelihoods have been plunged into desperation. They have repeatedly appealed for resumption of work and submitted petitions to the party and government for relief, but no definite measures have been taken. They request prompt assistance. They requested the Municipal Government to (1) order the factories to plan for resumption of work as soon as possible, and (2) provide food for the workers before work resumes. After hearing the situation, Secretary-General Yu expressed his utmost concern for the workers' suffering. Cause of Power Outage West of Kummen Road 146

Investigation revealed that a radio antenna line fell on a high-voltage overhead line. On the evening of the 11th of this month, there was a sudden power outage for one and a half hours in the area west of Kummen Road in the Shanghai West district. After investigation by the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, it was found that someone at the Chung Shan Tong Chinese Pharmacy, No. 2778 Chung Shan Road, was installing a radio antenna on the roof carelessly, causing the antenna to fall on the 33,000-volt high-voltage overhead line, resulting in a short circuit and power outage. The person installing the antenna was injured at the time and sent to the hospital. Public utilities are closely related to the lives of the people. If a failure occurs, a portion of the citizens will be inconvenienced. The general public must be extra careful with electrical circuits to avoid failures and endangering themselves.

Construction of Two Railway Lines, Completion of All Shanghai-Nanxiang Double Tracks 150

Two New Stations, Chung Shan Road and Hsinchiao, Added Along the Platforms, Reported to the Railway Department for Commencement of Traffic on April 1

The Two Railway Administration previously proposed to lay double tracks along the entire line in order to facilitate traffic due to the congestion of passenger transport on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. However, due to the huge cost of the project, they first started construction at Shanghai-Nanxiang. Since the start of construction last year, they have been working actively and spare no effort. Now, this project has been completed, and only a part of the gravel project is being rushed to completion. It is expected that it will be completed within days and traffic will begin. Therefore, travel between Shanghai and Nanxiang will be exclusively by small steam trains, which will borrow the vehicles currently running on the Songhu Railway and will be integrated with the Songhu Express. A new platform will be opened at the North Station specifically for these vehicles. It is also under construction. Two stations have now been decided to be added between Shanghai and Nanxiang, namely Chung Shan Road Station between Shanghai and Chenju (i.e., between Shanghai and Chenju), and Hsinchiao Station between Chennan (i.e., between Chenju and Nanxiang). The construction of these two stations will also be completed. The new stations are shaped like tram platforms, specifically for passengers to get on and off, and there is no office or ticket office. Tickets are sold on the train, and the fare is very low. The price from Shanghai directly to Nanxiang is only 25 cents, but there may be changes when traffic starts in the future. The Railway Department has already submitted detailed reports on the Yinghang train plan to the Ministry of Railways. It was originally planned to commence traffic on March 10, but because the instructions from the Ministry of Railways have not yet arrived, it will be necessary to wait until approval before setting the date for commencement of traffic. According to the Huadong News Agency reporter, it will start on April 1.

French Electricity and Water Company Robbery of Four Thousand Yuan Solved, French Police Arrested Eleven Robbers One After Another 152

On February 20 of this year, at 10:45 AM, Tu Chin-sheng, the compradore of the French Electricity and Water Tram Company at No. 249 Lupan Road in the French Concession, put 20,000 yuan in cash into two cloth bags, one containing 16,000 yuan and the other containing 4,000 yuan, and ordered Ch'in Jung-sheng (29 years old, from Changzhou), to take them out of the store and load them onto the company's own car to deposit them in a certain bank. Unexpectedly, as Ch'in carried the two bags out of the company's gate and stepped onto the car, four robbers suddenly rushed up, showed their pistols to intimidate him, and forbade him to make any noise. They robbed the cloth bag containing 4,000 yuan, carried the loot to a car pre-parked at the intersection of Kangti Road, and fled. The robbers fired two shots in the air as a warning before leaving. Later, the company reported the robbery to the French police and asked them to arrest the thieves and recover the stolen goods. Although detectives were dispatched to arrest the thieves, they were unable to apprehend them for a time. Until the evening of the 17th, the French police received a secret report from an informant through Chief Inspector Chin Chiu-lin of the Special Service Department, stating that the robbers who committed the robbery were hiding in a certain opium den in Fangchiao in the Chinese area, and the gang would definitely pass through Tafang Lane at 9:00 PM. Chief Inspector Chin immediately led detectives Tai Jung-chi, Chu Chu-tung, Wu Wen-kang, Hsu Yu-i, and Ma Yi-chih, together with detectives from the Public Security Bureau in charge of the area, and rushed to No. 25 Tafang Lane, Fangchiao at around 9:00 PM. They arrested the ringleader Ch'iu Yen-shou (24 years old, from Funing), Yang Yang (33 years old, from Chiangpei), and gang members Li Chung-hsin (24 years old, from Chiangpei) and Chu Han-chiang (28 years old, from Chiangpei). They confessed to robbing the French Electric Tram Company and committing multiple robberies in the French Concession. They also confessed that other accomplices were hiding in the New Tafang Hotel. The detectives sent the robbers to the Public Security Bureau and rushed to Rooms 8 and 14 of the New Tafang Hotel at No. 381 Aidoa Road to arrest gang members P'an Yu-ching (30 years old, from Hsu-chou), Liu Hsiao-ken (29 years old, from Changshu), Chang Te-piao (29 years old, from Muyang), Chao Chung-heng (34 years old, from Haichou), and Fan Yu-heng (32 years old, from Hsu-chou). They were taken to the police station and detained. Based on the confessions of the arrested robbers, they went to No. 30 Terh-run Lane, Nanshi Railway Station Road, and arrested the gang members Chou Kuei and Chou Lu, a married couple (the man is 25 years old and the woman is 27 years old, both from Chiangpei). They found two Browning pistols and sixteen bullets under the brick in the stove. They also went to No. 480 Fangsieh Road and arrested gang members Hsia Wen-fu (41 years old) and Hsu Yueh-cheng (37 years old), both from Chiangpei. They were sent to the Public Security Bureau and detained. The detectives worked all night and finished at 9:00 AM yesterday. Today, the five robbers arrested in the French Concession were sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation. They also asked the court to prepare a document to the Public Security Bureau to bring the eight male and female robbers detained there to court for detailed investigation.

Negotiation and Settlement Between the Press Association and Lien Hua Company 153

The Journalists Association's Three Demands Fully Accepted/The "New Woman" Film Has Been Edited

The Shanghai Press Association previously received a joint proposal from its members stating that the content of the "New Woman" film produced by Lien Hua Film Company insulted journalists. The Press Association negotiated with the company, and Mr. Wang Boch'i and Mr. Ma Yin-liang acted as mediators. Lien Hua Company fully accepted the three demands of the Press Association, and the matter has been satisfactorily resolved. The details are as follows:

Initiating Negotiations

On February 9, the Press Association convened a meeting of its Executive Committee to discuss how to deal with the insult to journalists in the "New Woman" film produced by Lien Hua Film Company. It appointed Chien Hua, Chin Hua-pai, Chiang Chia-tao, and Chien Shuo as representatives to negotiate with Lien Hua Company and resolved to make three demands to Lien Hua Company: (1) all insulting points in the film should be removed; (2) an apology should be published in the newspaper; and (3) a guarantee should be made that such incidents would not occur again in the future. The four representatives went back and forth to negotiate with the Lien Hua authorities. Lien Hua initially agreed to accept the principles and discuss the details, but then suddenly said that the Press Association should submit its demands in writing, implicitly indicating that the first and third demands were accepted and asking to avoid the second demand for a public apology. The initial negotiations thus came to an end. Afterwards, the Press Association sent a letter to Lien Hua, making three demands: (1) to remove the insulting points; (2) to publish an apology to journalists across the country in the newspaper; and (3) to guarantee that such incidents would not occur again in the future. It was also resolved to appoint Chien Hua, Chin Hsiung-pai, Chiang Tsung-tao, and Chien Ts'ang-shuo as representatives to negotiate with Lien Hua Company. However, Lien Hua replied with ambiguous wording, still hoping not to publish a public apology and accepting the first and second demands. After discussion at the joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Press Association on February 16, it was recognized that Lien Hua's reply was insincere. It was resolved to take further action, and negotiations broke down.

Formation of Special Case Committee

On February 17, the Press Association reconvened an emergency joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees and resolved to form a special case committee, appointing Yu K'ung-wo, Ch'u Shao-i, Yen Tu-ho, Chin Hsiung-pai, Chien Ts'ang-shuo, T'ang Shih-ch'ang, Chiang Tsung-tao, Chin Hua-t'ing, Chiang Ch'uang-hou, Hang Shih-chun, Ho Hsi-ya, Hsiang Yuan-ts'un, Chien Hua, Chao Chun-hao, and Sun Tao-sheng as the fifteen members of the committee responsible for handling the Lien Hua case and determining the principles to be followed.

Mediation

On February 22, Wu Pang-fan, the business director of Lien Hua Company, personally visited Mr. Ma Yin-liang, the manager of Shen Pao, asking him to mediate. Mr. Ma accompanied him to Mr. , who agreed to Lien Hua's request to serve as mediator. Wang and Ma, together with Wu Pang-fan, went to the Press Association to discuss a solution. After several rounds of consultation on the advertising text, it was decided that Lien Hua would publish the following advertisement: "Our company's 'New Woman' film had insertions of journalists, which caused dissatisfaction among the Shanghai Press Association. We are deeply grateful to Mr. Wang Boch'i and Mr. Ma Yin-liang for their willingness to mediate. We have now removed the inappropriate sections in the film and have satisfactorily resolved the matter. We hereby announce." In addition, the mediators published an advertisement stating, "Wang Boch'i and Ma Yin-liang's announcement on the negotiations between the Shanghai Press Association and Lien Hua Film Company: Lien Hua Film Company's 'New Woman' film had insertions of journalists, which caused dissatisfaction among the Shanghai Press Association. After mediation by us, the company has removed the inappropriate sections in the film and sent a letter of apology to the Press Association. The matter has now been satisfactorily resolved. This announcement." On the one hand, Lien Hua Company formally apologized to the Press Association in a letter and guaranteed that such incidents would not occur again in the future. The original letter said, "Dear Sirs, our company's 'New Woman' film had insertions of journalists, which caused dissatisfaction among your association. Our company sincerely apologizes. The three proposed measures of your association, apart from the first measure to remove the relevant sections and the third measure to guarantee that similar incidents will not occur again in the future, have already been declared in our previous letter of reply that we will comply with them. We hereby sincerely apologize. To the Shanghai Press Association."

The Editing Process

After the settlement of the negotiations, Lien Hua Company immediately edited the film. The Press Association appointed Chiang Chien-hou, Chin Hua-t'ing, Ho Hsi-ya, Chiang Tsung-tao, Huang T'ien-p'eng, and Chien Ts'ang-shuo as representatives. On March 14, at 10:00 AM, they gathered at the Central Grand Theater. Lien Hua Company gave a special screening of the edited "New Woman" film. After the representatives inspected it, they pointed out the points that should be supplemented and edited, and Lien Hua edited it again. The Press Association sent a letter to Lien Hua Company, agreeing that the unedited film would not be screened in theaters in this city or other cities in the future. This case was completely resolved.

Women's Organizations Send Letters to the Taxpayers' Association, Seriously Intervening in the Zhao Case 154

The Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association yesterday sent a letter to the German office of the Public Concession's Works Department, stating: "Respectfully, we have received letters with the seals of the Chinese Women's Sports League, the Chinese Women's Temperance Association, and the Shanghai YWCA, stating that newspapers have reported that English Constable Staff of Putuo Road beat to death a female vegetable vendor, Zhao, at Yichang Road. Widow Dies from Abortion 155

Ma Pan Denies Performing Abortion; Zhang Baiyong Detained Pending Verification

Zhang Baiyong, a 39-year-old man from Suzhou, worked at the Guangming Glass Car Side Factory. Recently, he became acquainted with a widow named Lu Fang, and they cohabitated at 156 North Fujian Road. After several intimate encounters, she became pregnant. Ms. Lu, being a widow, felt that being pregnant would be embarrassing, so she discussed it with Zhang. A few days ago, they hired Ma Pan, a 76-year-old midwife from Jiashan residing at 622 Chengda Lane, Tian Tong Road, to perform an abortion. After taking the medicine, the fetus was indeed aborted, but Ms. Lu experienced severe abdominal pain, which worsened daily. Zhang Baiyong was at a loss and, on the 15th of this month at 10 PM, sent her to the Tongren Hospital for treatment. However, she died before reaching the hospital. Upon examination, the hospital determined that she died from an abortion and reported it to the Huishi Police Station. Detective Tao Genrong and Western Detective Gibson were dispatched to take the body to the Philen Road autopsy center for examination. Midwife Ma Pan and Zhang Baiyong were arrested and detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The police station lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the situation, saying that the abortion fee was agreed upon at 35 yuan, with 18 yuan paid in advance. However, Ma Pan denied performing the abortion at the police station, claiming she only assisted with the birth and received 5 yuan. Since the autopsy had not yet been performed, he requested that Zhang and Ma be detained. Upon questioning, Ma Pan claimed that she was a midwife. Zhang hired her to go to his house, where she saw that it was a miscarriage. The child had already been born, but the placenta remained in the abdomen, and there was still unclean discharge, so she gave medicine to clear the discharge, receiving only 5 yuan. After Judge Qian Hongye questioned Zhang Baiyong briefly, he ordered Zhang to be detained until Friday for further questioning. Ma Pan was released on 500 yuan bail pending the autopsy. Meanwhile, Prosecutor Guo Wei arrived to examine the body and, after a brief inquiry, ruled that the deceased, Lu Fang, died from an abortion. Ma Pan and Zhang Baiyong were suspected of committing a crime and should be prosecuted by the police station in court. The body was handed over to the corpse caretaker, Lu Ni, who was instructed to prepare the coffin and burial.

Zhou Ronghui (also known as Ai Hua), a young woman from Jinshan in her early twenties, came to Shanghai from her hometown last February because her elder sister had married Wu Dajin and lived in Shanghai at 118 Dengtuo Road. She asked her brother-in-law to find her a job and stayed temporarily at Wu's house. Later, she occasionally went to see a movie at the Huade Grand Theatre, where she sat next to Zhu Dajun, a member of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps of Russian nationality. Zhu coveted Zhou's youth and beauty and took the opportunity to flirt with her. Zhou initially ignored him and quietly left her seat and returned home. However, Zhu was skilled in seduction and was not deterred by her rejection. Instead, he happily followed her, talking incessantly and boasting about his family background. When he saw Zhou's amorous glances, he intensified his offensive, eventually seducing Zhou. From then on, Zhou's chastity was violated. The Wugong Hotel on Fuzhou Road and the North Railway Station Hotel on Jielu Road were the havens for this pair of illicit lovers. Until last summer in July, Zhu's printing house was located far away at 61 Minhou South Lane, Hadong Road in West Shanghai. Meeting each other was inconvenient, and to save on travel expenses, they rented a house at 55 Zhengming Lane, Hede Road,

Cohabiting as Husband and Wife. Zhou was unmarried, and Zhu repeatedly claimed to have never been married, so they did not need the six rituals and immediately forged a bond for three lifetimes. Unexpectedly, on January 11 of this year, Zhu suddenly led a group of men and women into Zhou's bedroom, first violently beating her, then moving and taking away her clothes, and then leaving with his head high. Zhu has never returned since. Afterward, Zhou felt

Injured from the Beating, besides reporting to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, she cried and returned to her sister's house. Her brother-in-law, Wu Dajin, sent a letter to her mother, Zhou Zhang, asking her to rush to Shanghai to investigate. He found out that Zhu Dajun had already been married by his parents. The men and women who committed the assault were Zhu's parents and wife. Zhou Zhang felt that her daughter, Ai Hua, who was not yet twenty years old, had been seduced and defiled by Zhu and then humiliated by his gang beating her, which was intolerable. She was about to

File a Lawsuit, but Zhu struck first, filing a criminal self-lawsuit against Zhou for stealing and defrauding her of property, claiming that the woman was already twenty-three years old and that he had met her at Wing On Company. This time, taking advantage of his departure from Shanghai, she stole his watch, gold jewelry, silver dollars, and Volunteer Corps firearms. Zhou Ronghui, along with her mother, Zhou Zhang, hired lawyer Zhang Li to, in addition to

Defending Themselves According to Law, claiming that all the allegations made by Zhu were fabricated and requesting dismissal, filed a counterclaim, recounting the details of being seduced, defiled, and beaten by Zhu, demanding punishment according to the law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhan Liangce of the First Special District Court held a hearing to examine the original and defendant parties. First, Zhu Dajun stated the intention of his lawsuit. Then, Zhou Ronghui presented in court a letter of repentance written by Zhu himself, proving that she had been repeatedly beaten and abused by Zhu and that Zhu had no watch or gold jewelry. As for the firearms, Zhou stated that Zhu had accidentally dropped them when taking the items, and she had sent them to the police station. Judge Zhan ruled that Zhu Dajun had only sued Zhou Ronghui and had not included Zhou Zhang as a defendant, so Zhou Ronghui's counterclaim against Zhu Dajun was not necessary to be added as the plaintiff, and the portion of the counterclaim concerning disrupting the family did not fall under the jurisdiction of the primary court. These two points were rejected, and Zhu Dajun was ordered to post 200 yuan bail, and Zhou Ronghui was instructed to submit to a forensic examination for further investigation.

At Xujiahui Town, Shanghai West, the second post policeman Sun Wende of the Xuhui Police Station, was on duty on the sidewalk in front of Dechang South Goods Store in Xujiahui Town yesterday afternoon around 5 PM. I don't know in which year and by whom it was ceded to you. You can negotiate with our station. At that time, the onlookers were indignant. So far, the boundary has not been determined by superiors. In order to avoid disputes and maintain friendship between the two sides, the second post at that location has been temporarily moved to the sidewalk. Now it is not allowed to pass through the location and no post is allowed to be set up there. It is too much to force us to be under the corridor. Moreover, this area cannot abandon its duties. Before receiving orders, we will temporarily continue as before. As for the boundary, it will be clarified after the two sides confirm it.

Tang Yuqing, a native of Yancheng, used to cultivate land in his hometown. Because of the bankruptcy of the countryside, it was difficult to maintain a livelihood. He had no choice but to bring his wife, Sun, to Shanghai in 1920 to earn a living. They rented a house in Tanziwan, Zhabei. Tang made a living pulling a rickshaw, while Sun worked as a domestic helper. Although they were engaged in low-level work, they were still carefree and had no worries about food and clothing. In 1932, Tang Yuqing returned to his hometown on business. Unexpectedly, he never returned and there was no news from him. Sun was deeply anxious because she had not heard from him for a long time. There was a fellow villager, Zhou Cao, who was helping out in the neighboring house. They met day and night, so they knew each other and had a fellow villager relationship. They were exceptionally intimate and became close friends. Zhou Cao, because Sun's husband Tang Yuqing had been missing for a long time and Sun was living alone, thought there was an opportunity to take advantage of. So, she incited her in every way to remarry. Sun was ultimately young and allowed Zhou Cao to arrange things. In August of that year, with Zhou Cao's stockholders Fa Zhou Zaozhi and others as matchmakers, she remarried Cheng Yuqian, a puller from Funing, as his wife, and had a marriage certificate with a dowry of 120 yuan. More than three years passed. Now Tang Yuqing suddenly rushed to Cheng Yuqian's house and dragged Cheng and Sun to the police station. He also obtained the witness of Zhou Zaozhi (Zhou Cao's business partner Yin Changfa fled upon hearing the news) and brought them to the district court. Prosecutor Ouyang Shu's investigation was clear, and he prosecuted the criminal court for bigamy. Prosecutor Ouyang Shu also attended the court to argue. Finally, the defendant's lawyer Sun Wu rose and defended him. The judge considered the case concluded and scheduled the verdict to be announced at 2 PM on the 23rd of this month. The three defendants were sent back to jail to await instructions.

The deceased's father was still in the countryside, and the shop had sent a letter to notify him, saying that he could arrive in Shanghai today. Medical Community Observes: Yao Jinping is a Pseudo-Masculinized Female; A Similar Incident Occurred in Hangzhou Five Years Ago 163

The case of Yao Jinping, a woman from Tianjin who transformed into a man, has attracted the attention of all walks of life. Therefore, many people went to admire Yao's demeanor yesterday morning. At the same time, members of the medical community also went to visit.

Various Circles of Curiosity Compete to View

Yesterday morning, the citizens of this city, driven by curiosity, competed to view Yao Jinping, the woman who transformed into a man, at 18 Caitao Lane, Julu Road. There was a continuous stream of people. Yao's grandparents felt overwhelmed by the social calls. Gynecologist Dr. Mao Wenjie also went to Yao's residence at 10 AM yesterday to inquire. He requested an examination, but Yao, because her female form had not been completely eliminated and it had only been five months since the transformation, agreed to go to Mao's clinic for examination within this week.

The Male Organ is Slightly Different from Ordinary People

Mao then examined her by feeling through her pants. According to Mao's statement to the Huadong News Agency reporter, it is "female pseudohermaphroditism," which is commonly known as a female incubating a male. Yao's male organ, after it developed (i.e., after the transformation), is slightly different from ordinary men. It seems to have only a clitoris and no testicles. The penis is on the clitoris. The foreskin can be turned back and feels hard to the touch, but there is a lot of vaginal discharge, and the pants smell of a certain odor. Her breasts are larger on the right and smaller on the left, still in the form of a woman.

A Similar Incident Occurred in Hangzhou

According to Mao, in 1930, the Tongren Surgical Hospital on Qingnian Road in Hangzhou also had a Shaoxing person who was originally male, but suddenly fell seriously ill and found that his male organ had shrunk and had female physiological changes such as menstruation. Dr. Wang Jiren of the hospital used scientific methods to artificially create a female internal reproductive organ. After recovering from the illness, he returned to Shaoxing.

French Inspector-General Receives Yao and his Grandfather

After this incident occurred, Chinese and foreigners alike considered it a marvel. The French Concession Lujiiawan Police Station dispatched detectives to the General Police Station yesterday morning to have Yao and his grandfather questioned by Inspector-General Folangdeng (transliteration) about the transformation. After a long secret inquiry, they were ordered to withdraw. The details could not be ascertained because officials were not allowed to listen.

Will Return to Tianjin Within This Week

Yao came to Shanghai with his grandfather, Mr. Qingpu, at the invitation of General Li Du. Yao was eager to find his father and planned to follow the families of the anti-Japanese soldiers and transfer to Xinjiang in the shortest possible time to fulfill his wish to find his father ten thousand miles away. Now Li persuaded him to return to his original residence in Tianjin for further study, so it was decided that he would still be taken back to Tianjin by his grandfather within this week.

The View of Expert Wang Gu Ning

According to the Riri News Agency, Dr. Wang Gu Ning, a medical doctor from the Catholic University of Leuven in Belgium (specializing in pathological anatomy for more than 500 years), visited and requested an examination. Dr. Wang was the former surgeon at the Beijing Railway General Hospital and a neurologist at the Manchester Royal Hospital in England. He has a lot of experience in the study of the pathology of male and female physiology. According to him, the phenomenon of a woman turning into a man has already been studied by the medical community in the world. Many pathological anatomists have found (postmortem dissections) significant pathological conditions in the adrenal medulla and ovaries. The outer layer of adrenal tissue (Substance Corticale) is even more pronounced, so it is called adrenal masculinization (Virilisme Surrenalien). The onset of the transformation has no fixed symptoms, depending on age and temperate climates, and is closely related to physiology. According to scholars' observations, such pathological anatomical phenomena occur in five or six-year-old girls in temperate zones, whose genitals are like those of adult women, and menstruation also comes. If it belongs to a boy, with this disease, his genitals, physique, and psychology also become adult. If it belongs to an elderly woman, with this disease, her beard, voice, physique, etc., all become men. However, the external genitals become male, mostly belonging to young women who are about to become adults. The endocrine changes have been going on for a long time. Yao Jinping's transformation into a man upon hearing the sound of thunder is just a misperception or hallucination of that particular person, not a fact. There were also people like Yao Jinping in Europe in the past. In the police station, the gender on the residence permit was changed from female to male. However, in fact, the outside looks male, but the inside is still female. The reason for the change still needs detailed field research. Only in terms of the endocrine pathological anatomical abnormalities, or in addition to the above two types that have been proven, there should be many other pathologies that remain to be confirmed by physiology, pathology, anatomy, and other disciplines.

### New Proposals for Workers' Welfare by the Municipal Dock Business Office 167

The Municipal Dock Business Office, recognizing the extreme hardship of dockworkers' lives and their lack of attention to cleanliness and hygiene, which often leads to illness and death, has proposed to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Government the establishment of a public bathhouse for workers to improve their health. Furthermore, the office has recently learned that the Municipal Government is borrowing funds to build affordable housing and has submitted a proposal to the Municipal Government requesting that a portion of these funds be allocated to build a new village for dockworkers at Lannidujiao in Pudong, dedicated to dockworkers to facilitate training. Snippets 181

— (Ben Shui)

People often use the phrase "wearing colored glasses" to describe people who judge things with prejudice, but this is actually a mistake. When you first wear colored glasses, you may not be able to distinguish the colors; everything looks red through red glasses and green through green glasses. But over time, you gradually learn to distinguish all colors and will not confuse red and green. You can ask anyone who is used to wearing colored glasses.

Dr. Wegel of the United States calculated that the money spent on World War I, if lost at the rate of one US dollar per second since the time of Confucius, would be sixty dollars per minute, three thousand six hundred dollars per hour, and eighty-six thousand four hundred dollars per day. Even if this continued for the past two to three thousand years, the total would only be half of what was spent on the war. If we start losing money again now, it would probably take another two to three thousand years to lose the same amount as was spent on the war. The cost of war is truly staggering!

A Brief History of the Longhua Pagoda 182

— Zhang Muliang

Among the more than two thousand pagodas dotting China's landscape, Longhua is one of the most famous; hence, almost all Chinese people know it. The construction of pagodas originated in India, entering China with the eastward spread of Buddhism. It has been over 1,600 years since China has had pagodas. However, although the pagoda construction system originated in India, the Chinese, with their ingenuity, have innovated designs that are very different from Indian pagodas. Moreover, geomancers consider them related to Feng Shui, and the whole world has followed suit, resulting in pagodas spreading throughout various regions. The pagoda styles in different parts of China are not uniform. Southern pagodas are superior in form and color, while northern pagodas appear simpler, often lacking carved railings in their corridors. However, their construction is extremely solid, with spiral staircases inside leading to the top. The height of pagodas varies from seven to thirteen levels, with the tallest pagoda in Dingzhou, Zhili, reaching 360 feet.

Over time, most of the earliest pagodas have collapsed and no longer exist. Those seen today, although some still stand majestically on their original sites, are mostly reconstructions from later periods. The Ming and Qing dynasties saw countless pagoda reconstructions. However, the construction of the Longhua Pagoda predates the Ming Dynasty by several centuries. According to the Shanghai County Annals, it was initially built during the Three Kingdoms period. At that time, Emperor Da of Wu controlled the Jiangbiao region, extending west to Wuchang and south to Minyue, possessing abundant resources. The pagoda stood for over 400 years until the Tang Dynasty, when it was renovated and the adjacent temple was named Longhua Temple, thus fixing the pagoda's name. Not long after, Huang Chao's rebellion destroyed both the temple and the pagoda by fire. It was not until more than 200 years later that the Qian family established the state in this area, known as Wuyue. When King Zhongyi ascended the throne, he ordered Zhuang Wu to have Zhang Rentai oversee the reconstruction. It is said that King Zhongyi, while sailing on the Huangpu River, anchored in the river at night and saw a light in the sky, shining at the site of the old pagoda, which he considered an auspicious sign, hence the order. The pagoda that stands tall today as a landmark of Shanghai is this one.

Rain Song in the Capital 183

— Shi Duan

As soon as it rains, a lot of mud squeezes onto the roads. Where do they hide on sunny days? It's really strange. As soon as pedestrians step out, these nasty little things cling tightly to your feet, making you feel particularly disgusted, just like ordinary people hate those arrogant bigwigs. This is a unique flavor of Nanjing in the rain. I have been to Hangzhou, to Shanghai... but there is nothing more unpleasant than a rainy day in Nanjing. As soon as I see dark clouds spreading, my heart is lightly pressed with a layer of aversion.

Originally, Nanjing is mostly desolate and quiet. Once drizzled with sorrowful rain, Nanjing immediately sinks further into a lonely well. I ask those who have been to Nanjing, what impression did the rain give them?

Those cars, once it rains, rush wildly across the streets, speeding arbitrarily, and the sounds of their horns are so arrogant, especially on rainy days, it is simply a threat to all the lonely rickshaws or horse carriages.

The rain in Nanjing, I feel terrible just thinking about it. What's terrible is those muds that I don't know where they hide on sunny days, and after the rain, they immediately squeeze onto the roads to confront pedestrians' feet. But I also thought of a short story by Tolstoy: "The Waves of Freedom." Although the mud is small, it also has its perseverance and freedom (life). How can we ignore them, great life!

Flint Vendor 184

— Zhu Shaofei

When I was a child, while helping my grandmother start the fire and cook, she would sometimes say to me, "The flint is used up, baby. Listen for the flint vendor, call him to buy a new one." I liked hearing this in my little ears. The next day, I would carefully listen for the "ta-la-ta" sound, because this was a great opportunity for me to buy a clay Buddha figurine to play with. Usually, my grandmother would rarely buy me toys, so the only hope I had was when buying new flint, I dared to ask to buy one to play with. That's why I paid close attention to the flint vendor when I was a child.

The flint vendors from Jiangbei would row a small boat to our Dongshan. The men would always be leatherworkers, and the women would carry flint baskets to sell flint in the villages. They would hold two clam shells in their fingers, knocking them together with a "ta-la-ta" sound. They not only sold flint but also collected shoes to have their husbands put soles on them. According to my grandmother, the clay Buddha figurines were newly added when I was learning to walk.

Flint was gradually defeated by matches, and they added needles and thread to their baskets. But recently, when I returned to my hometown, the goods in their baskets had changed again. Besides needles and thread, they had almost become general merchandise vendors, adding socks, stockings, handkerchiefs, rouge, and cosmetics. What stung my eyes the most was that clay Buddha figurines were rarely seen, replaced by toys from some country with English writing on them. Here, I saw that the women in our remote Dongshan were also learning to be fashionable, and I also felt that the omnipresent toys from some country had also penetrated my hometown.

Professional Front 185

The Women's Paradise

Husband and Wife Dialogue 186

— Zhang Huang

In the daily conversations between husband and wife, sometimes one party needs to express empty comfort — just like the so-called "lip service," only to adapt to the environment; the other party, however, hopes that you will show this little comfort at the appropriate time, and they will feel grateful and content! This does not mean that there should be any false affection between loving partners living together, but it all relies on this little procedure to connect and integrate the inspirations of both parties, which cannot be avoided. Otherwise, often even if you are trying your best to do practical work of consolation, because you don't scratch the itch, you still can't get the other party's comfort or sympathy. Just look: "In the Changmen Palace, no dressing up all day, why bother with pearls to soothe loneliness?" A bushel of bright pearls only gets unexpected few lines of resentful poetry in return, isn't it not worth it!

Also, sometimes a request made by one party is satisfied just by getting a verbal permission from the other party, and there is no real need to see it implemented; because that request — whether it is giving or accepting — only serves the purpose of testing love or probing sympathy. Under such circumstances, you can't avoid casually going along with it, and rest assured that there will be no difficulties following.

For example, one day, the wife was hurriedly putting on makeup before going out, and she shouted anxiously because she couldn't draw her eyebrows to her satisfaction: "Why can't I draw them well no matter how I try!"

At this time, the husband was dealing with other things on the side, and he chimed in and said, "Let me draw them for you."

"Okay," the wife replied, while continuing to draw them herself, without stopping to wait for her husband to come and help. But strangely, the situation suddenly turned smoothly, and she quickly completed her work; she felt very satisfied!

Just imagine, when the wife was feeling frustrated and couldn't help but shout it out, how anxious she was in her heart! If the husband was afraid of further disturbing her work and remained silent, wouldn't this silent environment cause her to misunderstand, thinking that he was deliberately standing by and not wanting to help? By saying this, "Let me draw them for you," at least the wife knows that he cares about her beauty! Moreover, a husband drawing his wife's eyebrows has always been recognized as a joy in the boudoir; such a romantic and considerate impression, once awakened by him, will produce an incredible effect of regulating bad emotions and comforting her heart! Does it matter whether things are actually done or not?

As for the sentence "Let me draw them for you," which you casually say but contains a request; he himself may not be sure whether he can quickly and effectively take over this eyebrow-drawing task. The wife also knows this situation, and may even know that he will definitely not be able to do it well, and her original intention is really not to cause more trouble for him; but how can she directly and frankly refuse his courteous offer? She had no choice but to casually respond, as if accepting his kindness. In this way, her good habit of not being aggressive when she is upset shows her extreme love for her husband, and at the same time, his comfort can make her mood more peaceful, and her eyebrows are finally drawn!

The tiniest details of what husband and wife hear are related to how grand the environment is. I advise all married people that these things are really not to be ignored!

The two novels today should be switched with those of yesterday, specifically for correction.

The Misty Records of the Imperial Incense 187

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Although I was so nostalgic, according to what I later discovered, these girls who were careful about raising silkworms—most of them were daughters of bannermen—really liked silkworms; so sleeping with silkworm eggs in their arms was commonplace and not worth fussing about.

While I was vaguely imagining what it was like to sleep with silkworm eggs in my arms, the Empress Dowager spoke again.

"Look! Aren't these newly hatched?" She went to another corner of the room. "But they grow very quickly, you can almost watch them grow; in about seven or eight days, they will start feeding on large mulberry leaves."

Here, several wooden shelves were placed with many round, low plates, which were made of bamboo, and part of the bottom of the plates was made of very smooth bamboo pith; their edges were about an inch and a half high and were also tied with bamboo strips. These bamboo plates were different in size, and must have had different uses. As I saw it, the newly hatched silkworms were nothing more than small green worms that could be seen on flowers and trees, and they were very ugly; the only difference was that they had no patterns on their bodies, but were covered in gray and white. They were probably seven or eight tenths of an inch long, and a small bamboo plate was crowded with about one or two hundred of them; they were squirming, and I almost mistook them for a plate of maggots.

Although I didn't think these silkworms were good-looking at all, and even thought they were very ugly, because I heard the Empress Dowager say that they grew very quickly, and I could almost watch them grow, my curiosity was aroused (270)

Sports News

Next Year's World Games: The Olympic Village is Declared Established; the Village Has Dormitories and Training Grounds for 3,000 Athletes; All Kinds of Equipment Will Be Completed by May 1st of Next Year 188

(Berlin Special Dispatch) The large-scale Olympic Village currently is the one scheduled for Los Angeles, North America, in 1932. Germany must fulfill its obligations and treat the competitors from all countries in the world equally for the 1936 World Games (Olympic Games) to fulfill its responsibility of completing the World Games. The German National Defense Army is also prepared to bear the auxiliary capacity of this responsibility to build the Olympic Village and maintain its various administrations.

We imagine that the National Defense Army's great interest in the Games will ensure that all preparations are properly made so that all foreign guests arriving in Germany can have a model residence here that satisfies their desires.

The new Olympic Village is fourteen kilometers away from the Republican Sports Field. The undulating forest here is a landmark of Brandenburg with excellent scenery. As for this Games, it is expected that there will be 3,000 participants. The village has dormitories and training grounds. The women's sector will be separately arranged by the Olympic Committee at the Republican Sports Field. There has been an enthusiastic response from all over the world for those now requesting accommodation in the Olympic Village. The German Olympic Committee is handling the construction of the Olympic Village based on the experience gained in North America. The German Committee certainly cannot but consider the situation in Germany, estimate the large number of participants this time, and determine the location of the Olympic Village and manage its climate.

All the foundation, roads, and various development matters in the village can be fully completed in 1935. By 1935, various tall buildings should also be completed on schedule. The installation of all kinds of equipment can be completed by May 1, 1936. The entrance to the Olympic Village has a reception room, in front of which there is a large open space leading directly to Berlin Hamburg Street. The arrangements in the reception room are able to meet the needs of all guests and committee members. There are reception rooms, offices for the leaders of various delegations, telephones, the Republican Auditorium, storage of money, transportation offices, banks, post offices, and shops, etc. In addition, there are restaurants prepared for the guests of each competitor. However, guests who want to visit the competitors in the village—as stipulated by the North American Olympic Games—this is greatly beneficial to the competitors, so it is not allowed to enter the village directly. Near the entrance to the village is the dormitory area. There are many dormitories in the village, forming a large ring. However, the dormitories are all single-story stone buildings, each with ten to twelve rooms, all equipped with washing machines and shower irrigators. Each room is three meters wide and four meters long and has two beds. To the north of the village is a large business office with forty kitchens and dining halls, each with various equipment, such as kitchen administration, washing, food supply, fire protection, and parking facilities.

There are quite a few bathrooms in the village, and there is also a barber shop. The sports field itself is equipped with a public assembly hall according to the standards of the Olympic competition line, which also has a gymnasium for athletes to practice. Near the hall there is a large swimming pool, which embellishes the entire facility. In the center of the village is the judge's office, with a cluster of gleaming birch trees protruding. Preparations have now begun to make the accommodation in this village comfortable. This business has been entrusted to the German Shipping Company, which has a wealth of international experience. The cost of bathing, food, and car fare is six marks per person per day and night. In addition, to protect the safety of foreign guests, it is stipulated that each country can have German youth athletes as noble guards. These guards have a good understanding of the languages of various countries.

In order to integrate foreign guests of the 1936 Winter Games with the domestic people, people in the hotel industry and other people can freely come to take English and French lessons. To expand the plan, English or French lectures must also be promoted in primary and secondary schools.

The Thirteenth Guangdong Provincial Games 190

Scheduled to be held for ten days starting May 4th; Preparatory Committee established, passed the Games Regulations

The 13th Guangdong Provincial Games has been scheduled to be held at the Guangzhou Public Sports Field on May 4th of this year. The Provincial Sports Committee has been instructed by the Education Department to cooperate with the Guangzhou Municipal Government to send personnel to prepare. The budget was originally set at 30,000 yuan, with 10,000 yuan allocated by the Provincial Government, and the rest supplemented by the Municipal Government, and expenses were covered by athletes' registration fees, entrance ticket prices, and stall rental fees in the field. Yesterday, three standing committee members sent by the Provincial Sports Committee and three people appointed by the Municipal Government as members of the Games Organizing Committee held their first preparatory meeting on the 13th. The Games Regulations were revised and passed, and it was decided that the 13th Games will open on May 4th and end on the 13th, lasting for ten consecutive days. Registration begins immediately and ends on April 18th. This year's Games will not have a team overall championship or an individual venue champion. Those with excellent sports performance, the top three in the competition category, track and field events, and various ball games will be awarded medals. Performers will be awarded certificates. Athletes with outstanding results will be selected to represent the province at the National Games in Shanghai on Double Ten Festival this year. The Provincial Games this year will still have a county league category. To facilitate the participation of various counties and save time and money, the county league has been advanced to be held from May 4th to 7th, while the Provincial Games will be held from the 8th to the 13th. The Games are initiated by the Provincial and Municipal Governments and jointly organized by the Provincial Sports Association and various sectors. A number of honorary chairmen, one chairman, two vice-chairmen, seven senior judges, and a number of consultants are set up. In addition, an audit department, a general affairs department, a finance department, a competition department, an arrangement department, a public relations department, a publicity department, a discipline department, and a security department are set up, each with one director and a number of members. The sports categories of the Games have also been stipulated as follows: (1) Competitive events: (A) Track events, hurdles, 110-meter high hurdles, 400-meter intermediate hurdles (above, men's team A), 80-meter low hurdles (above, men's team B, women's team A), freehand running, 50 meters (women's team A and B), 100 meters (men's team A and B, women's team A and B), 200 meters (men's team A and B, women's team A and B), 400 meters (men's team A and B, women's team A and B), 800 meters, 1,500 meters, 10,000 meters (men's, no teams), (B) Field events, pole vault (men's team A and B), freehand high jump (men's team A and B, women's team A and B), freehand long jump (men's team A and B, women's team A and B), triple jump (men's team A and B, women's team A and B), shot put (men's team A and B, women's team A and B, men's A 12 pounds, team B 12 pounds, women's A 10 pounds, women's B 6 pounds), discus throw, javelin (men's and women's, no teams), indoor softball throw (women's team A and B), (C) All-around, relay race, 200 meters (women's team A and B), 400 meters (men's team A and B, women's team A and B), 1,600 meters (men's team A and B, women's no teams), five-event total, ten-event total (men's no teams), (D) Ball games, Group A volleyball (men's and women's, but no teams), Group B volleyball (men's team B), Group A soccer (men's no teams), Group B soccer (men's team B), Group A basketball (men's and women's, but no teams), Group B basketball (men's team B), doubles and singles tennis (men's and women's, but no teams), softball (men's no teams), indoor softball (women's no teams), table tennis (men's and women's, but no teams), (2) Performance items, joint performances, including national flag exercises, thousand-person exercises, thousand-person dances, scout drills, military drills, group performances, including general exercises, games, martial arts, free performances (March 13th)

Education News

This City to Launch Literacy Education Program 201

Literacy Textbook Being Edited by the Education Bureau, Literacy Education Committee to Be Established Soon

Preparations for the large-scale literacy education movement in this city have been reported in newspapers many times. It is now known that the Municipal Education Bureau is actively preparing for this work and will organize a Literacy Education Committee to be specifically responsible for it. The organizational outline of the committee has also been drafted. Details are listed below:

Active Preparations: There are many illiterate people in this city. Conducting literacy education is a very large undertaking. The budget is estimated at 200,000 yuan, which will be allocated by the municipal government. It is planned to hold six sessions of adult classes, each session lasting two months, and three sessions of children's classes, each session lasting four months, tentatively for one year. It is planned to start classes in June. The first step is to investigate the design and edit textbooks. The investigation work is the responsibility of the Public Security Bureau and has already begun. However, this work cannot be completed in a short period of time. Therefore, the Education Bureau has now allocated the number of schools to be established in each district. There are a total of seventeen districts, including the whole province, Shanghai South, and Zhabei. Each district is divided into several small areas, and each small area will be assigned a number of schools as appropriate, totaling at least more than 300 schools in the city. However, in the special zone, it is planned to use social education groups and cultural institutions to promote this work.

Editing Textbooks: As for editing textbooks, the Education Bureau has organized a People's School Reader Committee to be responsible for editing textbooks for both adults and children. After several discussions, they are nearing completion. It is named the Shanghai Municipal Citizens' Literacy Textbook. The content temporarily completes sixteen lessons of the citizen part, twelve lessons of the nature part, twelve lessons of the social part, and eight lessons of the health part, with a vocabulary of about 618 characters. The initial draft personnel for each part have also been decided. The first eight lessons will be edited by Li Wanyu, the citizen lessons will be edited by Xie Engao, the nature lessons will be edited by Zhang Yongchun, the social lessons will be edited by Chen Songshu, the health lessons will be edited by Hu Changcai, and the review lessons will be edited by Zhang Zhu. It has been decided that the initial draft will be submitted on the 20th of this month. Regarding the drawing of illustrations, Shi Chongpeng, Ji Xiaobo, Zhang Meisun, and Shi Lianhuang and others will discuss and set the date for drawing illustrations from April 1st to 15th.

Organizational Outline: The detailed outline of the organization of the Shanghai Municipal Literacy Education Committee. Article 1: This committee is organized based on the Ministry of Education's implementation of the adult supplementary education plan, taking into account the actual situation of illiterate people in this city. Article 2: The committee will consist of fifteen members, who will be appointed by the municipal government from the following personnel: 1. The mayor, 2. The director of the Education Bureau, 3. The director of the Public Security Bureau, 4. The director of the Social Affairs Bureau, 5. Three representatives of the Municipal Party Headquarters, 6. The section chief in charge of the Municipal Government, 7. The section chief in charge of the Public Security Bureau, 9. The supervisor of the Education Bureau. Article 3: The mayor will be the chairman of the committee, and the director of the Education Bureau will be the vice chairman. A standing committee will be established with three standing committee members (to be taken up by the section chief in charge of the Education Bureau supervisor, or the section chief in charge of the Public Security Bureau). Article 4: The committee will have a number of clerks, who will be transferred from the municipal government and the bureaus. Article 5: The committee will have three sections for design, investigation, and inspection. The detailed rules for its operation will be set separately. The matters that the committee should handle are as follows: 1. Plan the overall literacy education program for the city, 2. Plan the implementation steps of the city's mass literacy education, 3. Allocate the funds, time, location, class sessions, etc. for the city's mass literacy education, 4. Examine and approve the textbooks and supplementary readings used for the city's mass literacy education, 5. Plan the methods for selecting teachers for the city's mass literacy education, 6. Inspect and supervise the progress of mass literacy training, 7. Other matters that should be planned and handled. Article 6: The committee will hold a regular meeting once a month, and special meetings may be held when necessary, all convened by the chairman of the committee. Article 7: The committee may organize various temporary committees when necessary to handle various special matters. The detailed rules for this will be set separately. Article 8: The resolutions of the committee will be handled separately by the relevant sections in charge of the Education Bureau. Article 9: The funds for the committee will be allocated by the municipal government. Article 10: The committee will be attached to the Education Bureau. Article 11: This committee will be dissolved when mass literacy education is widespread throughout the city. Article 12: This outline will be promulgated and implemented after being approved by the municipal government and filed with the Ministry of Education.

###庚款 Funds to Promote Compulsory Education, Ministry of Education Discusses and Determines Methods

Informing the Gengkuan Committee

(Nanjing, 18th) The Third Joint Conference on Gengkuan Funds resolved to jointly launch new educational undertakings, of which 800,000 yuan will be used to promote compulsory education. At the same time, the National Government should allocate a considerable amount from the central funding for the next year as a subsidy for compulsory education. Recently, the Ministry of Education drafted an outline of measures to subsidize remote and impoverished provinces in implementing compulsory education, which was submitted to the Executive Yuan and then to the 448th meeting of the Central Political Conference for approval, and handed over to the Budget Review Committee. The Ministry of Education sent a letter recording the main points of the outline of the measures, requesting the four Gengkuan Fund agencies of China-US, China-UK, China-Belgium, and China-France to take note. The main points are as follows: 1. The provinces to be subsidized are temporarily limited to Shaanxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, Ningxia, Qinghai, Chahar, Suiyuan, Gansu, Xinjiang, and Xikang. 2. The subsidy amount is 75,000 yuan from the national treasury each year, totaling 750,000 yuan. Its designated uses are: 1. Adding compulsory primary schools, 2. Adding short-term primary schools, 3. Strengthening existing primary schools, 4. Adding or expanding rural normal schools, 5. Subsidizing the promotion of schools. The two departments are planning to establish compulsory education experimental zones.

National Beiyang Institute of Technology to Reduce Tuition for New Students 204

The National Beiyang Institute of Technology recently recognized that the rural economy is depressed and children from farming families are reluctant to advance their studies. Reducing various fees is necessary to seek relief. Following the 39th Institute Affairs Conference, it was decided that from the admission of new students in the 24th year of the Republic, tuition fees will be 10 yuan per semester, a reduction of 5 yuan from the previous amount. The originally stipulated accommodation fee of 6 yuan per semester and the one-time library fee of 15 yuan paid upon entering the school have been completely abolished. The sports fee of 1 yuan per semester and the compensation fee (i.e., security deposit) of 10 yuan remain the same. In addition, the application fee has been reduced from 3 yuan to 1 yuan. These measures have been submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval and filing. It is noted that the institute has always been known for its simplicity. Students focus on academics and have no frivolous or romantic habits, so personal expenses are very low. After this reduction, each person only needs 200 yuan per year, which can be said to be the lowest cost among all national universities.

The Ministry of Education recently compiled statistics on the number of schools, students, and funding for secondary schools in various provinces and cities in the 20th year of the Republic, and provided a detailed analysis of the number of middle schools, vocational schools, and normal schools. Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education Visits the Jiangsu Education College in Suzhou 206

Lecturing on Mass Education Issues and Visiting the Achievement Exhibition

Wuxi Jiangsu Provincial Education College held its eighth achievement exhibition on the 15th, 16th, and 17th of this month, and celebrated the seventh anniversary of its founding. The grand occasion was unprecedented in recent years. The Ministry of Education first sent Director Jiong of the Department of Social Education to the college on the 15th to visit and inspect. Minister Wang, accompanied by Director Lei Zhen of the General Affairs Department, former President Yang Zhensheng of the National Qingdao University, and Mr. Chen Zikuan of the Wuxi Industrial Machinery Factory, personally visited on the afternoon of the 17th to inspect the case. They highly praised the college's facilities and various achievements at the exhibition. Starting at 2:00 PM, they lectured on mass education issues in the college's auditorium, hoping that all teachers and students would not regard mass education as too difficult, nor too easy, and especially need to have a full sense of service and strive to establish mass education academics, so that mass education becomes scientific, rather than just common sense. The words were concise and comprehensive. In total, more than 10,000 people visited in three days, especially many local people. Well-known figures in the social education field, such as Liang Shuming, Peng Baichuan, Xiang Jutan, and Shu Xincheng, Wu Bangni, and others also came to Wuxi from afar to visit. Mr. Qian Tianhe, director of the Central Agricultural Experiment Station, lectured on the problem of Chinese agricultural research experiments at the college on the morning of the 16th, and there were many listeners. Furthermore, the situation of this exhibition at the college, in terms of achievements, included static displays, administrative statistics, educational effects, various charts, educational tools, student achievements, etc., and dynamic performances, with college students performing musical performances, speech contests, and drama performances, etc. In addition, there were competitions among the local people in the various experimental institutions, singing, language education, speech, fire fighting skills, and recreation performances, and sports meets. The achievements were significantly better than before. As for the exhibition section, it was divided into college history, the Department of Academic Affairs, the Department of Research and Experiment, the Library, the Experimental Workshop, the Biological Experiment Room, the Insect Experiment Room, the Mass Science Museum, the Radio Broadcasting Station, Chinese Painting, Applied Painting, Western Painting, Agricultural Science Crafts, Chicken Bee, Pig, Dairy Cow Farm, Agricultural Chemistry Experiment Room, Crop Experiment Room, Crop Area, Horticultural Area, Hospital, etc. The various experimental institutions, including the two experimental areas of Huibei and Beixia, the Nanmen People's Education Center, and the Experimental People's School, also had some achievements. The achievements displayed in the college, but most of the achievements, People's Schools, Rural Improvement Association, various cooperatives, agricultural warehouses, mobile teaching, model families, shed education, labor education, rural autonomy, etc., are all within the various teaching areas. The number of people who went to visit in the three days was particularly large. Zhou, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, specially sent film technician Zhang Jingshi to Wuxi to shoot films of various achievements and activities exhibited, so as to promote the development of mass education.

Enrolling Students on April 1st

(Nanjing, 18th) The Sericulture Specialist School, directed by Dr. Marie of the Economic Council's Sericulture Improvement Association, is enrolling students in Nanjing. The Academic Work Advisory Center is handling the enrollment. Anyone registered at the Nanjing headquarters of the Work Advisory Center and the Shanghai branch can take the exam. Registration will be from April 1st to 8th. Those who have registered can apply at the center during the registration period. The entrance exam will be held separately in Nanjing and Shanghai on April 10th, and 40 students will be admitted. The study period is two years. Those who have not completed their studies will be sent to work in various institutions under the association. During the study period, tuition and accommodation fees are waived. Scholarships of 50 to 200 yuan per year will be given to each student according to their academic performance.

Chen Qingtao Goes to Japan to Study Dentistry 208

Mr. Chen Qingtao, a native of Zhongshan County, Guangdong, is the chairman of the Dental Association of this city and the second son of Chen Weiqing. After graduating from the high school department of Datong University in this city, he specialized in Japanese in preparation for studying dentistry in Japan. He has now boarded a ship on the 18th to go to Japan and will study at the Tokyo Dental Medical School, which is the most prestigious in Japan, for four years.

Finally, Zhu Shaoping spoke freely about his observations and feelings during his trip to South Africa. The meeting lasted for three hours before it dispersed.
